8 // ----
9 // CUDA C/C++ includes memory space designation as variable type qualifers (such ----
10 // as __global__ and __shared__). Knowing the space of a memory access allows ----
11 // CUDA compilers to emit faster PTX loads and stores. For example, a load from ----
12 // shared memory can be translated to `ld.shared` which is roughly 10% faster ----
13 // than a generic `ld` on an NVIDIA Tesla K40c. ----
14 // ----
15 // Unfortunately, type qualifiers only apply to variable declarations, so CUDA ----
16 // compilers must infer the memory space of an address expression from ----
17 // type-qualified variables. ----
18 // ----
19 // LLVM IR uses non-zero (so-called) specific address spaces to represent memory ----
20 // spaces (e.g. addrspace(3) means shared memory). The Clang frontend ----
21 // places only type-qualified variables in specific address spaces, and then ----
22 // conservatively `addrspacecast`s each type-qualified variable to addrspace(0) ----
23 // (so-called the generic address space) for other instructions to use. ----
24 // ----
25 // For example, the Clang translates the following CUDA code ----
26 // __shared__ float a[10]; ----
27 // float v = a[i]; ----
28 // to ----
29 // %0 = addrspacecast [10 x float] addrspace(3)* @a to [10 x float]* ----
30 // %1 = gep [10 x float], [10 x float]* %0, i64 0, i64 %i ----
31 // %v = load float, float* %1 ; emits ld.f32 ----
32 // @a is in addrspace(3) since it's type-qualified, but its use from %1 is ----
33 // redirected to %0 (the generic version of @a). ----
34 // ----
35 // The optimization implemented in this file propagates specific address spaces ----
36 // from type-qualified variable declarations to its users. For example, it ----
37 // optimizes the above IR to ----
38 // %1 = gep [10 x float] addrspace(3)* @a, i64 0, i64 %i ----
39 // %v = load float addrspace(3)* %1 ; emits ld.shared.f32 ----
40 // propagating the addrspace(3) from @a to %1. As the result, the NVPTX ----
41 // codegen is able to emit ld.shared.f32 for %v. ----
42 // ----
43 // Address space inference works in two steps. First, it uses a data-flow ----
44 // analysis to infer as many generic pointers as possible to point to only one ----
45 // specific address space. In the above example, it can prove that %1 only ----
46 // points to addrspace(3). This algorithm was published in ----
47 // CUDA: Compiling and optimizing for a GPU platform ----
48 // Chakrabarti, Grover, Aarts, Kong, Kudlur, Lin, Marathe, Murphy, Wang ----
49 // ICCS 2012 ----
50 // ----
51 // Then, address space inference replaces all refinable generic pointers with ----
52 // equivalent specific pointers. ----
53 // ----
54 // The major challenge of implementing this optimization is handling PHINodes, ----
55 // which may create loops in the data flow graph. This brings two complications. ----
56 // ----
57 // First, the data flow analysis in Step 1 needs to be circular. For example, ----
58 // %generic.input = addrspacecast float addrspace(3)* %input to float* ----
59 // loop: ----
60 // %y = phi [ %generic.input, %y2 ] ----
61 // %y2 = getelementptr %y, 1 ----
62 // %v = load %y2 ----
63 // br ..., label %loop, ... ----
64 // proving %y specific requires proving both %generic.input and %y2 specific, ----
65 // but proving %y2 specific circles back to %y. To address this complication, ----
66 // the data flow analysis operates on a lattice: ----
67 // uninitialized > specific address spaces > generic. ----
68 // All address expressions (our implementation only considers phi, bitcast, ----
69 // addrspacecast, and getelementptr) start with the uninitialized address space. ----
70 // The monotone transfer function moves the address space of a pointer down a ----
71 // lattice path from uninitialized to specific and then to generic. A join ----
72 // operation of two different specific address spaces pushes the expression down ----
73 // to the generic address space. The analysis completes once it reaches a fixed ----
74 // point. ----
75 // ----
76 // Second, IR rewriting in Step 2 also needs to be circular. For example, ----
77 // converting %y to addrspace(3) requires the compiler to know the converted ----
78 // %y2, but converting %y2 needs the converted %y. To address this complication, ----
79 // we break these cycles using "poison" placeholders. When converting an ----
80 // instruction `I` to a new address space, if its operand `Op` is not converted ----
81 // yet, we let `I` temporarily use `poison` and fix all the uses later. ----
82 // For instance, our algorithm first converts %y to ----
83 // %y' = phi float addrspace(3)* [ %input, poison ] ----
84 // Then, it converts %y2 to ----
85 // %y2' = getelementptr %y', 1 ----
86 // Finally, it fixes the poison in %y' so that ----
87 // %y' = phi float addrspace(3)* [ %input, %y2' ] ----
88 // ----
89 //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===// ----

265 // Check whether that's no-op pointer bicast using a pair of ----
266 // `ptrtoint`/`inttoptr` due to the missing no-op pointer bitcast over ----
267 // different address spaces. ----
268 static bool isNoopPtrIntCastPair(const Operator *I2P, const DataLayout &DL, 0
269 const TargetTransformInfo *TTI) { ----
270 assert(I2P->getOpcode() == Instruction::IntToPtr); 0
271 auto *P2I = dyn_cast(I2P->getOperand(0)); 0
272 if (!P2I || P2I->getOpcode() != Instruction::PtrToInt) 0
273 return false; 0
274 // Check it's really safe to treat that pair of `ptrtoint`/`inttoptr` as a ----
275 // no-op cast. Besides checking both of them are no-op casts, as the ----
276 // reinterpreted pointer may be used in other pointer arithmetic, we also ----
277 // need to double-check that through the target-specific hook. That ensures ----
278 // the underlying target also agrees that's a no-op address space cast and ----
279 // pointer bits are preserved. ----
280 // The current IR spec doesn't have clear rules on address space casts, ----
281 // especially a clear definition for pointer bits in non-default address ----
282 // spaces. It would be undefined if that pointer is dereferenced after an ----
283 // invalid reinterpret cast. Also, due to the unclearness for the meaning of ----
284 // bits in non-default address spaces in the current spec, the pointer ----
285 // arithmetic may also be undefined after invalid pointer reinterpret cast. ----
286 // However, as we confirm through the target hooks that it's a no-op ----
287 // addrspacecast, it doesn't matter since the bits should be the same. ----
288 unsigned P2IOp0AS = P2I->getOperand(0)->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace(); 0
289 unsigned I2PAS = I2P->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace(); 0
290 return CastInst::isNoopCast(Instruction::CastOps(I2P->getOpcode()), 0
291 I2P->getOperand(0)->getType(), I2P->getType(), ----
292 DL) && 0
293 CastInst::isNoopCast(Instruction::CastOps(P2I->getOpcode()), 0
294 P2I->getOperand(0)->getType(), P2I->getType(), ----
295 DL) && 0
296 (P2IOp0AS == I2PAS || TTI->isNoopAddrSpaceCast(P2IOp0AS, I2PAS)); 0
297 } ----

299 // Returns true if V is an address expression. ----
300 // TODO: Currently, we consider only phi, bitcast, addrspacecast, and ----
301 // getelementptr operators. ----
302 static bool isAddressExpression(const Value &V, const DataLayout &DL, 0
303 const TargetTransformInfo *TTI) { ----
304 const Operator *Op = dyn_cast(&V); 0
305 if (!Op) 0
306 return false; 0
307 ----
308 switch (Op->getOpcode()) { 0
309 case Instruction::PHI: 0
310 assert(Op->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()); 0
311 return true; 0
312 case Instruction::BitCast: 0
313 case Instruction::AddrSpaceCast: ----
314 case Instruction::GetElementPtr: ----
315 return true; 0
316 case Instruction::Select: 0
317 return Op->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy(); 0
318 case Instruction::Call: { 0
319 const IntrinsicInst *II = dyn_cast(&V); 0
320 return II && II->getIntrinsicID() == Intrinsic::ptrmask; 0
321 } ----
322 case Instruction::IntToPtr: 0
323 return isNoopPtrIntCastPair(Op, DL, TTI); 0
324 default: 0
325 // That value is an address expression if it has an assumed address space. ----
326 return TTI->getAssumedAddrSpace(&V) != UninitializedAddressSpace; 0
327 } ----
328 } ----

330 // Returns the pointer operands of V. ----
331 // ----
332 // Precondition: V is an address expression. ----
333 static SmallVector ----
334 getPointerOperands(const Value &V, const DataLayout &DL, 0
335 const TargetTransformInfo *TTI) { ----
336 const Operator &Op = cast(V); 0
337 switch (Op.getOpcode()) { 0
338 case Instruction::PHI: { 0
339 auto IncomingValues = cast(Op).incoming_values(); 0
340 return {IncomingValues.begin(), IncomingValues.end()}; 0
341 } ----
342 case Instruction::BitCast: 0
343 case Instruction::AddrSpaceCast: ----
344 case Instruction::GetElementPtr: ----
345 return {Op.getOperand(0)}; 0
346 case Instruction::Select: 0
347 return {Op.getOperand(1), Op.getOperand(2)}; 0
348 case Instruction::Call: { 0
349 const IntrinsicInst &II = cast(Op); 0
350 assert(II.getIntrinsicID() == Intrinsic::ptrmask && 0
351 "unexpected intrinsic call"); ----
352 return {II.getArgOperand(0)}; 0
353 } ----
354 case Instruction::IntToPtr: { 0
355 assert(isNoopPtrIntCastPair(&Op, DL, TTI)); 0
356 auto *P2I = cast(Op.getOperand(0)); 0
357 return {P2I->getOperand(0)}; 0
358 } ----
359 default: 0
360 llvm_unreachable("Unexpected instruction type."); 0
361 } ----
362 } ----

364 bool InferAddressSpacesImpl::rewriteIntrinsicOperands(IntrinsicInst *II, 0
365 Value *OldV, ----
366 Value *NewV) const { ----
367 Module *M = II->getParent()->getParent()->getParent(); 0
368 ----
369 switch (II->getIntrinsicID()) { 0
370 case Intrinsic::objectsize: { 0
371 Type *DestTy = II->getType(); 0
372 Type *SrcTy = NewV->getType(); 0
373 Function *NewDecl = ----
374 Intrinsic::getDeclaration(M, II->getIntrinsicID(), {DestTy, SrcTy}); 0
375 II->setArgOperand(0, NewV); 0
376 II->setCalledFunction(NewDecl); 0
377 return true; 0
378 } ----
379 case Intrinsic::ptrmask: 0
380 // This is handled as an address expression, not as a use memory operation. ----
381 return false; 0
382 case Intrinsic::masked_gather: { 0
383 Type *RetTy = II->getType(); 0
384 Type *NewPtrTy = NewV->getType(); 0
385 Function *NewDecl = ----
386 Intrinsic::getDeclaration(M, II->getIntrinsicID(), {RetTy, NewPtrTy}); 0
387 II->setArgOperand(0, NewV); 0
388 II->setCalledFunction(NewDecl); 0
389 return true; 0
390 } ----
391 case Intrinsic::masked_scatter: { 0
392 Type *ValueTy = II->getOperand(0)->getType(); 0
393 Type *NewPtrTy = NewV->getType(); 0
394 Function *NewDecl = ----
395 Intrinsic::getDeclaration(M, II->getIntrinsicID(), {ValueTy, NewPtrTy}); 0
396 II->setArgOperand(1, NewV); 0
397 II->setCalledFunction(NewDecl); 0
398 return true; 0
399 } ----
400 default: { 0
401 Value *Rewrite = TTI->rewriteIntrinsicWithAddressSpace(II, OldV, NewV); 0
402 if (!Rewrite) 0
403 return false; 0
404 if (Rewrite != II) 0
405 II->replaceAllUsesWith(Rewrite); 0
406 return true; 0
407 } ----
408 } ----
409 } ----

411 void InferAddressSpacesImpl::collectRewritableIntrinsicOperands( 0
412 IntrinsicInst *II, PostorderStackTy &PostorderStack, ----
413 DenseSet &Visited) const { ----
414 auto IID = II->getIntrinsicID(); 0
415 switch (IID) { 0
416 case Intrinsic::ptrmask: 0
417 case Intrinsic::objectsize: ----
418 appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack(II->getArgOperand(0), 0
419 PostorderStack, Visited); ----
420 break; 0
421 case Intrinsic::masked_gather: 0
422 appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack(II->getArgOperand(0), 0
423 PostorderStack, Visited); ----
424 break; 0
425 case Intrinsic::masked_scatter: 0
426 appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack(II->getArgOperand(1), 0
427 PostorderStack, Visited); ----
428 break; 0
429 default: 0
430 SmallVector OpIndexes; 0
431 if (TTI->collectFlatAddressOperands(OpIndexes, IID)) { 0
432 for (int Idx : OpIndexes) { 0
433 appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack(II->getArgOperand(Idx), 0
434 PostorderStack, Visited); ----
435 } ----
436 } ----
437 break; 0
438 } ----
439 } 0

441 // Returns all flat address expressions in function F. The elements are ----
442 // If V is an unvisited flat address expression, appends V to PostorderStack ----
443 // and marks it as visited. ----
444 void InferAddressSpacesImpl::appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack( 0
445 Value *V, PostorderStackTy &PostorderStack, ----
446 DenseSet &Visited) const { ----
447 assert(V->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()); 0
448 ----
449 // Generic addressing expressions may be hidden in nested constant ----
450 // expressions. ----
451 if (ConstantExpr *CE = dyn_cast(V)) { 0
452 // TODO: Look in non-address parts, like icmp operands. ----
453 if (isAddressExpression(*CE, *DL, TTI) && Visited.insert(CE).second) 0
454 PostorderStack.emplace_back(CE, false); 0
455 ----
456 return; 0
457 } ----
458 ----
459 if (V->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == FlatAddrSpace && 0
460 isAddressExpression(*V, *DL, TTI)) { 0
461 if (Visited.insert(V).second) { 0
462 PostorderStack.emplace_back(V, false); 0
463 ----
464 Operator *Op = cast(V); 0
465 for (unsigned I = 0, E = Op->getNumOperands(); I != E; ++I) { 0
466 if (ConstantExpr *CE = dyn_cast(Op->getOperand(I))) { 0
467 if (isAddressExpression(*CE, *DL, TTI) && Visited.insert(CE).second) 0
468 PostorderStack.emplace_back(CE, false); 0
469 } ----
470 } ----
471 } ----
472 } ----
473 } ----

475 // Returns all flat address expressions in function F. The elements are ordered ----
476 // ordered in postorder. ----
477 std::vector ----
478 InferAddressSpacesImpl::collectFlatAddressExpressions(Function &F) const { 0
479 // This function implements a non-recursive postorder traversal of a partial ----
480 // use-def graph of function F. ----
481 PostorderStackTy PostorderStack; 0
482 // The set of visited expressions. ----
483 DenseSet Visited; 0
484 ----
485 auto PushPtrOperand = [&](Value *Ptr) { 0
486 appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack(Ptr, PostorderStack, 0
487 Visited); 0
488 }; 0
489 ----
490 // Look at operations that may be interesting accelerate by moving to a known ----
491 // address space. We aim at generating after loads and stores, but pure ----
492 // addressing calculations may also be faster. ----
493 for (Instruction &I : instructions(F)) { 0
494 if (auto *GEP = dyn_cast(&I)) { 0
495 PushPtrOperand(GEP->getPointerOperand()); 0
496 } else if (auto *LI = dyn_cast(&I)) 0
497 PushPtrOperand(LI->getPointerOperand()); 0
498 else if (auto *SI = dyn_cast(&I)) 0
499 PushPtrOperand(SI->getPointerOperand()); 0
500 else if (auto *RMW = dyn_cast(&I)) 0
501 PushPtrOperand(RMW->getPointerOperand()); 0
502 else if (auto *CmpX = dyn_cast(&I)) 0
503 PushPtrOperand(CmpX->getPointerOperand()); 0
504 else if (auto *MI = dyn_cast(&I)) { 0
505 // For memset/memcpy/memmove, any pointer operand can be replaced. ----
506 PushPtrOperand(MI->getRawDest()); 0
507 ----
508 // Handle 2nd operand for memcpy/memmove. ----
509 if (auto *MTI = dyn_cast(MI)) 0
510 PushPtrOperand(MTI->getRawSource()); 0
511 } else if (auto *II = dyn_cast(&I)) 0
512 collectRewritableIntrinsicOperands(II, PostorderStack, Visited); 0
513 else if (ICmpInst *Cmp = dyn_cast(&I)) { 0
514 if (Cmp->getOperand(0)->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()) { 0
515 PushPtrOperand(Cmp->getOperand(0)); 0
516 PushPtrOperand(Cmp->getOperand(1)); 0
517 } ----
518 } else if (auto *ASC = dyn_cast(&I)) { 0
519 PushPtrOperand(ASC->getPointerOperand()); 0
520 } else if (auto *I2P = dyn_cast(&I)) { 0
521 if (isNoopPtrIntCastPair(cast(I2P), *DL, TTI)) 0
522 PushPtrOperand( 0
523 cast(I2P->getOperand(0))->getOperand(0)); 0
524 } ----
525 } ----
526 ----
527 std::vector Postorder; // The resultant postorder. 0
528 while (!PostorderStack.empty()) { 0
529 Value *TopVal = PostorderStack.back().getPointer(); 0
530 // If the operands of the expression on the top are already explored, ----
531 // adds that expression to the resultant postorder. ----
532 if (PostorderStack.back().getInt()) { 0
533 if (TopVal->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == FlatAddrSpace) 0
534 Postorder.push_back(TopVal); 0
535 PostorderStack.pop_back(); 0
536 continue; 0
537 } ----
538 // Otherwise, adds its operands to the stack and explores them. ----
539 PostorderStack.back().setInt(true); 0
540 // Skip values with an assumed address space. ----
541 if (TTI->getAssumedAddrSpace(TopVal) == UninitializedAddressSpace) { 0
542 for (Value *PtrOperand : getPointerOperands(*TopVal, *DL, TTI)) { 0
543 appendsFlatAddressExpressionToPostorderStack(PtrOperand, PostorderStack, 0
544 Visited); ----
545 } 0
546 } ----
547 } ----
548 return Postorder; 0
549 } 0
550 ----
551 // A helper function for cloneInstructionWithNewAddressSpace. Returns the clone ----
552 // of OperandUse.get() in the new address space. If the clone is not ready yet, ----
553 // returns poison in the new address space as a placeholder. ----
554 static Value *operandWithNewAddressSpaceOrCreatePoison( 0
555 const Use &OperandUse, unsigned NewAddrSpace, ----
556 const ValueToValueMapTy &ValueWithNewAddrSpace, ----
557 const PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy &PredicatedAS, ----
558 SmallVectorImpl *PoisonUsesToFix) { ----
559 Value *Operand = OperandUse.get(); 0
560 ----
561 Type *NewPtrTy = getPtrOrVecOfPtrsWithNewAS(Operand->getType(), NewAddrSpace); 0
562 ----
563 if (Constant *C = dyn_cast(Operand)) 0
564 return ConstantExpr::getAddrSpaceCast(C, NewPtrTy); 0
565 ----
566 if (Value *NewOperand = ValueWithNewAddrSpace.lookup(Operand)) 0
567 return NewOperand; 0
568 ----
569 Instruction *Inst = cast(OperandUse.getUser()); 0
570 auto I = PredicatedAS.find(std::make_pair(Inst, Operand)); 0
571 if (I != PredicatedAS.end()) { 0
572 // Insert an addrspacecast on that operand before the user. ----
573 unsigned NewAS = I->second; 0
574 Type *NewPtrTy = getPtrOrVecOfPtrsWithNewAS(Operand->getType(), NewAS); 0
575 auto *NewI = new AddrSpaceCastInst(Operand, NewPtrTy); 0
576 NewI->insertBefore(Inst); 0
577 NewI->setDebugLoc(Inst->getDebugLoc()); 0
578 return NewI; 0
579 } ----
580 ----
581 PoisonUsesToFix->push_back(&OperandUse); 0
582 return PoisonValue::get(NewPtrTy); 0
583 } ----
584 ----
585 // Returns a clone of `I` with its operands converted to those specified in ----
586 // ValueWithNewAddrSpace. Due to potential cycles in the data flow graph, an ----
587 // operand whose address space needs to be modified might not exist in ----
588 // ValueWithNewAddrSpace. In that case, uses poison as a placeholder operand and ----
589 // adds that operand use to PoisonUsesToFix so that caller can fix them later. ----
590 // ----
591 // Note that we do not necessarily clone `I`, e.g., if it is an addrspacecast ----
592 // from a pointer whose type already matches. Therefore, this function returns a ----
593 // Value* instead of an Instruction*. ----
594 // ----
595 // This may also return nullptr in the case the instruction could not be ----
596 // rewritten. ----
597 Value *InferAddressSpacesImpl::cloneInstructionWithNewAddressSpace( 0
598 Instruction *I, unsigned NewAddrSpace, ----
599 const ValueToValueMapTy &ValueWithNewAddrSpace, ----
600 const PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy &PredicatedAS, ----
601 SmallVectorImpl *PoisonUsesToFix) const { ----
602 Type *NewPtrType = getPtrOrVecOfPtrsWithNewAS(I->getType(), NewAddrSpace); 0
603 ----
604 if (I->getOpcode() == Instruction::AddrSpaceCast) { 0
605 Value *Src = I->getOperand(0); 0
606 // Because `I` is flat, the source address space must be specific. ----
607 // Therefore, the inferred address space must be the source space, according ----
608 // to our algorithm. ----
609 assert(Src->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == NewAddrSpace); 0
610 if (Src->getType() != NewPtrType) 0
611 return new BitCastInst(Src, NewPtrType); 0
612 return Src; 0
613 } ----
614 ----
615 if (IntrinsicInst *II = dyn_cast(I)) { 0
616 // Technically the intrinsic ID is a pointer typed argument, so specially ----
617 // handle calls early. ----
618 assert(II->getIntrinsicID() == Intrinsic::ptrmask); 0
619 Value *NewPtr = operandWithNewAddressSpaceOrCreatePoison( 0
620 II->getArgOperandUse(0), NewAddrSpace, ValueWithNewAddrSpace, 0
621 PredicatedAS, PoisonUsesToFix); ----
622 Value *Rewrite = ----
623 TTI->rewriteIntrinsicWithAddressSpace(II, II->getArgOperand(0), NewPtr); 0
624 if (Rewrite) { 0
625 assert(Rewrite != II && "cannot modify this pointer operation in place"); 0
626 return Rewrite; 0
627 } ----
628 ----
629 return nullptr; 0
630 } ----
631 ----
632 unsigned AS = TTI->getAssumedAddrSpace(I); 0
633 if (AS != UninitializedAddressSpace) { 0
634 // For the assumed address space, insert an `addrspacecast` to make that ----
635 // explicit. ----
636 Type *NewPtrTy = getPtrOrVecOfPtrsWithNewAS(I->getType(), AS); 0
637 auto *NewI = new AddrSpaceCastInst(I, NewPtrTy); 0
638 NewI->insertAfter(I); 0
639 return NewI; 0
640 } ----
641 ----
642 // Computes the converted pointer operands. ----
643 SmallVector NewPointerOperands; 0
644 for (const Use &OperandUse : I->operands()) { 0
645 if (!OperandUse.get()->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()) 0
646 NewPointerOperands.push_back(nullptr); 0
647 else ----
648 NewPointerOperands.push_back(operandWithNewAddressSpaceOrCreatePoison( 0
649 OperandUse, NewAddrSpace, ValueWithNewAddrSpace, PredicatedAS, ----
650 PoisonUsesToFix)); ----
651 } ----
652 ----
653 switch (I->getOpcode()) { 0
654 case Instruction::BitCast: 0
655 return new BitCastInst(NewPointerOperands[0], NewPtrType); 0
656 case Instruction::PHI: { 0
657 assert(I->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()); 0
658 PHINode *PHI = cast(I); 0
659 PHINode *NewPHI = PHINode::Create(NewPtrType, PHI->getNumIncomingValues()); 0
660 for (unsigned Index = 0; Index < PHI->getNumIncomingValues(); ++Index) { 0
661 unsigned OperandNo = PHINode::getOperandNumForIncomingValue(Index); 0
662 NewPHI->addIncoming(NewPointerOperands[OperandNo], 0
663 PHI->getIncomingBlock(Index)); ----
664 } ----
665 return NewPHI; 0
666 } ----
667 case Instruction::GetElementPtr: { 0
668 GetElementPtrInst *GEP = cast(I); 0
669 GetElementPtrInst *NewGEP = GetElementPtrInst::Create( 0
670 GEP->getSourceElementType(), NewPointerOperands[0], 0
671 SmallVector(GEP->indices())); 0
672 NewGEP->setIsInBounds(GEP->isInBounds()); 0
673 return NewGEP; 0
674 } ----
675 case Instruction::Select: 0
676 assert(I->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()); 0
677 return SelectInst::Create(I->getOperand(0), NewPointerOperands[1], 0
678 NewPointerOperands[2], "", nullptr, I); 0
679 case Instruction::IntToPtr: { 0
680 assert(isNoopPtrIntCastPair(cast(I), *DL, TTI)); 0
681 Value *Src = cast(I->getOperand(0))->getOperand(0); 0
682 if (Src->getType() == NewPtrType) 0
683 return Src; 0
684 ----
685 // If we had a no-op inttoptr/ptrtoint pair, we may still have inferred a ----
686 // source address space from a generic pointer source need to insert a cast ----
687 // back. ----
688 return CastInst::CreatePointerBitCastOrAddrSpaceCast(Src, NewPtrType); 0
689 } ----
690 default: 0
691 llvm_unreachable("Unexpected opcode"); 0
692 } ----
693 } 0
694 ----
695 // Similar to cloneInstructionWithNewAddressSpace, returns a clone of the ----
696 // constant expression `CE` with its operands replaced as specified in ----
697 // ValueWithNewAddrSpace. ----
698 static Value *cloneConstantExprWithNewAddressSpace( 0
699 ConstantExpr *CE, unsigned NewAddrSpace, ----
700 const ValueToValueMapTy &ValueWithNewAddrSpace, const DataLayout *DL, ----
701 const TargetTransformInfo *TTI) { ----
702 Type *TargetType = ----
703 CE->getType()->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy() 0
704 ? getPtrOrVecOfPtrsWithNewAS(CE->getType(), NewAddrSpace) 0
705 : CE->getType(); 0
706 ----
707 if (CE->getOpcode() == Instruction::AddrSpaceCast) { 0
708 // Because CE is flat, the source address space must be specific. ----
709 // Therefore, the inferred address space must be the source space according ----
710 // to our algorithm. ----
711 assert(CE->getOperand(0)->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == 0
712 NewAddrSpace); ----
713 return ConstantExpr::getBitCast(CE->getOperand(0), TargetType); 0
714 } ----
715 ----
716 if (CE->getOpcode() == Instruction::BitCast) { 0
717 if (Value *NewOperand = ValueWithNewAddrSpace.lookup(CE->getOperand(0))) 0
718 return ConstantExpr::getBitCast(cast(NewOperand), TargetType); 0
719 return ConstantExpr::getAddrSpaceCast(CE, TargetType); 0
720 } ----
721 ----
722 if (CE->getOpcode() == Instruction::IntToPtr) { 0
723 assert(isNoopPtrIntCastPair(cast(CE), *DL, TTI)); 0
724 Constant *Src = cast(CE->getOperand(0))->getOperand(0); 0
725 assert(Src->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == NewAddrSpace); 0
726 return ConstantExpr::getBitCast(Src, TargetType); 0
727 } ----
728 ----
729 // Computes the operands of the new constant expression. ----
730 bool IsNew = false; 0
731 SmallVector NewOperands; 0
732 for (unsigned Index = 0; Index < CE->getNumOperands(); ++Index) { 0
733 Constant *Operand = CE->getOperand(Index); 0
734 // If the address space of `Operand` needs to be modified, the new operand ----
735 // with the new address space should already be in ValueWithNewAddrSpace ----
736 // because (1) the constant expressions we consider (i.e. addrspacecast, ----
737 // bitcast, and getelementptr) do not incur cycles in the data flow graph ----
738 // and (2) this function is called on constant expressions in postorder. ----
739 if (Value *NewOperand = ValueWithNewAddrSpace.lookup(Operand)) { 0
740 IsNew = true; 0
741 NewOperands.push_back(cast(NewOperand)); 0
742 continue; 0
743 } ----
744 if (auto *CExpr = dyn_cast(Operand)) 0
745 if (Value *NewOperand = cloneConstantExprWithNewAddressSpace( 0
746 CExpr, NewAddrSpace, ValueWithNewAddrSpace, DL, TTI)) { ----
747 IsNew = true; 0
748 NewOperands.push_back(cast(NewOperand)); 0
749 continue; 0
750 } ----
751 // Otherwise, reuses the old operand. ----
752 NewOperands.push_back(Operand); 0
753 } ----
754 ----
755 // If !IsNew, we will replace the Value with itself. However, replaced values ----
756 // are assumed to wrapped in an addrspacecast cast later so drop it now. ----
757 if (!IsNew) 0
758 return nullptr; 0
759 ----
760 if (CE->getOpcode() == Instruction::GetElementPtr) { 0
761 // Needs to specify the source type while constructing a getelementptr ----
762 // constant expression. ----
763 return CE->getWithOperands(NewOperands, TargetType, /*OnlyIfReduced=*/false, 0
764 cast(CE)->getSourceElementType()); 0
765 } ----
766 ----
767 return CE->getWithOperands(NewOperands, TargetType); 0
768 } 0
769 ----
770 // Returns a clone of the value `V`, with its operands replaced as specified in ----
771 // ValueWithNewAddrSpace. This function is called on every flat address ----
772 // expression whose address space needs to be modified, in postorder. ----
773 // ----
774 // See cloneInstructionWithNewAddressSpace for the meaning of PoisonUsesToFix. ----
775 Value *InferAddressSpacesImpl::cloneValueWithNewAddressSpace( 0
776 Value *V, unsigned NewAddrSpace, ----
777 const ValueToValueMapTy &ValueWithNewAddrSpace, ----
778 const PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy &PredicatedAS, ----
779 SmallVectorImpl *PoisonUsesToFix) const { ----
780 // All values in Postorder are flat address expressions. ----
781 assert(V->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == FlatAddrSpace && 0
782 isAddressExpression(*V, *DL, TTI)); ----
783 ----
784 if (Instruction *I = dyn_cast(V)) { 0
785 Value *NewV = cloneInstructionWithNewAddressSpace( 0
786 I, NewAddrSpace, ValueWithNewAddrSpace, PredicatedAS, PoisonUsesToFix); ----
787 if (Instruction *NewI = dyn_cast_or_null(NewV)) { 0
788 if (NewI->getParent() == nullptr) { 0
789 NewI->insertBefore(I); 0
790 NewI->takeName(I); 0
791 NewI->setDebugLoc(I->getDebugLoc()); 0
792 } ----
793 } ----
794 return NewV; 0
795 } ----
796 ----
797 return cloneConstantExprWithNewAddressSpace( 0
798 cast(V), NewAddrSpace, ValueWithNewAddrSpace, DL, TTI); 0
799 } ----
800 ----
801 // Defines the join operation on the address space lattice (see the file header ----
802 // comments). ----
803 unsigned InferAddressSpacesImpl::joinAddressSpaces(unsigned AS1, 0
804 unsigned AS2) const { ----
805 if (AS1 == FlatAddrSpace || AS2 == FlatAddrSpace) 0
806 return FlatAddrSpace; 0
807 ----
808 if (AS1 == UninitializedAddressSpace) 0
809 return AS2; 0
810 if (AS2 == UninitializedAddressSpace) 0
811 return AS1; 0
812 ----
813 // The join of two different specific address spaces is flat. ----
814 return (AS1 == AS2) ? AS1 : FlatAddrSpace; 0
815 } ----
816 ----
817 bool InferAddressSpacesImpl::run(Function &F) { 0
818 DL = &F.getParent()->getDataLayout(); 0
819 ----
820 if (AssumeDefaultIsFlatAddressSpace) 0
821 FlatAddrSpace = 0; 0
822 ----
823 if (FlatAddrSpace == UninitializedAddressSpace) { 0
824 FlatAddrSpace = TTI->getFlatAddressSpace(); 0
825 if (FlatAddrSpace == UninitializedAddressSpace) 0
826 return false; 0
827 } ----
828 ----
829 // Collects all flat address expressions in postorder. ----
830 std::vector Postorder = collectFlatAddressExpressions(F); 0
831 ----
832 // Runs a data-flow analysis to refine the address spaces of every expression ----
833 // in Postorder. ----
834 ValueToAddrSpaceMapTy InferredAddrSpace; 0
835 PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy PredicatedAS; 0
836 inferAddressSpaces(Postorder, InferredAddrSpace, PredicatedAS); 0
837 ----
838 // Changes the address spaces of the flat address expressions who are inferred ----
839 // to point to a specific address space. ----
840 return rewriteWithNewAddressSpaces(Postorder, InferredAddrSpace, PredicatedAS, 0
841 &F); 0
842 } 0
843 ----
844 // Constants need to be tracked through RAUW to handle cases with nested ----
845 // constant expressions, so wrap values in WeakTrackingVH. ----
846 void InferAddressSpacesImpl::inferAddressSpaces( 0
847 ArrayRef Postorder, ----
848 ValueToAddrSpaceMapTy &InferredAddrSpace, ----
849 PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy &PredicatedAS) const { ----
850 SetVector Worklist(Postorder.begin(), Postorder.end()); 0
851 // Initially, all expressions are in the uninitialized address space. ----
852 for (Value *V : Postorder) 0
853 InferredAddrSpace[V] = UninitializedAddressSpace; 0
854 ----
855 while (!Worklist.empty()) { 0
856 Value *V = Worklist.pop_back_val(); 0
857 ----
858 // Try to update the address space of the stack top according to the ----
859 // address spaces of its operands. ----
860 if (!updateAddressSpace(*V, InferredAddrSpace, PredicatedAS)) 0
861 continue; 0
862 ----
863 for (Value *User : V->users()) { 0
864 // Skip if User is already in the worklist. ----
865 if (Worklist.count(User)) 0
866 continue; 0
867 ----
868 auto Pos = InferredAddrSpace.find(User); 0
869 // Our algorithm only updates the address spaces of flat address ----
870 // expressions, which are those in InferredAddrSpace. ----
871 if (Pos == InferredAddrSpace.end()) 0
872 continue; 0
873 ----
874 // Function updateAddressSpace moves the address space down a lattice ----
875 // path. Therefore, nothing to do if User is already inferred as flat (the ----
876 // bottom element in the lattice). ----
877 if (Pos->second == FlatAddrSpace) 0
878 continue; 0
879 ----
880 Worklist.insert(User); 0
881 } ----
882 } ----
883 } 0
884 ----
885 unsigned InferAddressSpacesImpl::getPredicatedAddrSpace(const Value &V, 0
886 Value *Opnd) const { ----
887 const Instruction *I = dyn_cast(&V); 0
888 if (!I) 0
889 return UninitializedAddressSpace; 0
890 ----
891 Opnd = Opnd->stripInBoundsOffsets(); 0
892 for (auto &AssumeVH : AC.assumptionsFor(Opnd)) { 0
893 if (!AssumeVH) 0
894 continue; 0
895 CallInst *CI = cast(AssumeVH); 0
896 if (!isValidAssumeForContext(CI, I, DT)) 0
897 continue; 0
898 ----
899 const Value *Ptr; ----
900 unsigned AS; ----
901 std::tie(Ptr, AS) = TTI->getPredicatedAddrSpace(CI->getArgOperand(0)); 0
902 if (Ptr) 0
903 return AS; 0
904 } ----
905 ----
906 return UninitializedAddressSpace; 0
907 } ----
908 ----
909 bool InferAddressSpacesImpl::updateAddressSpace( 0
910 const Value &V, ValueToAddrSpaceMapTy &InferredAddrSpace, ----
911 PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy &PredicatedAS) const { ----
912 assert(InferredAddrSpace.count(&V)); 0
913 ----
914 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "Updating the address space of\n " << V << '\n'); 0
915 ----
916 // The new inferred address space equals the join of the address spaces ----
917 // of all its pointer operands. ----
918 unsigned NewAS = UninitializedAddressSpace; 0
919 ----
920 const Operator &Op = cast(V); 0
921 if (Op.getOpcode() == Instruction::Select) { 0
922 Value *Src0 = Op.getOperand(1); 0
923 Value *Src1 = Op.getOperand(2); 0
924 ----
925 auto I = InferredAddrSpace.find(Src0); 0
926 unsigned Src0AS = (I != InferredAddrSpace.end()) ? 0
927 I->second : Src0->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace(); 0
928 ----
929 auto J = InferredAddrSpace.find(Src1); 0
930 unsigned Src1AS = (J != InferredAddrSpace.end()) ? 0
931 J->second : Src1->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace(); 0
932 ----
933 auto *C0 = dyn_cast(Src0); 0
934 auto *C1 = dyn_cast(Src1); 0
935 ----
936 // If one of the inputs is a constant, we may be able to do a constant ----
937 // addrspacecast of it. Defer inferring the address space until the input ----
938 // address space is known. ----
939 if ((C1 && Src0AS == UninitializedAddressSpace) || 0
940 (C0 && Src1AS == UninitializedAddressSpace)) 0
941 return false; 0
942 ----
943 if (C0 && isSafeToCastConstAddrSpace(C0, Src1AS)) 0
944 NewAS = Src1AS; 0
945 else if (C1 && isSafeToCastConstAddrSpace(C1, Src0AS)) 0
946 NewAS = Src0AS; 0
947 else ----
948 NewAS = joinAddressSpaces(Src0AS, Src1AS); 0
949 } else { ----
950 unsigned AS = TTI->getAssumedAddrSpace(&V); 0
951 if (AS != UninitializedAddressSpace) { 0
952 // Use the assumed address space directly. ----
953 NewAS = AS; 0
954 } else { ----
955 // Otherwise, infer the address space from its pointer operands. ----
956 for (Value *PtrOperand : getPointerOperands(V, *DL, TTI)) { 0
957 auto I = InferredAddrSpace.find(PtrOperand); 0
958 unsigned OperandAS; ----
959 if (I == InferredAddrSpace.end()) { 0
960 OperandAS = PtrOperand->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace(); 0
961 if (OperandAS == FlatAddrSpace) { 0
962 // Check AC for assumption dominating V. ----
963 unsigned AS = getPredicatedAddrSpace(V, PtrOperand); 0
964 if (AS != UninitializedAddressSpace) { 0
965 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() 0
966 << " deduce operand AS from the predicate addrspace " ----
967 << AS << '\n'); ----
968 OperandAS = AS; 0
969 // Record this use with the predicated AS. ----
970 PredicatedAS[std::make_pair(&V, PtrOperand)] = OperandAS; 0
971 } ----
972 } ----
973 } else ----
974 OperandAS = I->second; 0
975 ----
976 // join(flat, *) = flat. So we can break if NewAS is already flat. ----
977 NewAS = joinAddressSpaces(NewAS, OperandAS); 0
978 if (NewAS == FlatAddrSpace) 0
979 break; 0
980 } 0
981 } ----
982 } ----
983 ----
984 unsigned OldAS = InferredAddrSpace.lookup(&V); 0
985 assert(OldAS != FlatAddrSpace); 0
986 if (OldAS == NewAS) 0
987 return false; 0
988 ----
989 // If any updates are made, grabs its users to the worklist because ----
990 // their address spaces can also be possibly updated. ----
991 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << " to " << NewAS << '\n'); 0
992 InferredAddrSpace[&V] = NewAS; 0
993 return true; 0
994 } ----
995 ----
996 /// \p returns true if \p U is the pointer operand of a memory instruction with ----
997 /// a single pointer operand that can have its address space changed by simply ----
998 /// mutating the use to a new value. If the memory instruction is volatile, ----
999 /// return true only if the target allows the memory instruction to be volatile ----
1000 /// in the new address space. ----
1001 static bool isSimplePointerUseValidToReplace(const TargetTransformInfo &TTI, 0
1002 Use &U, unsigned AddrSpace) { ----
1003 User *Inst = U.getUser(); 0
1004 unsigned OpNo = U.getOperandNo(); 0
1005 bool VolatileIsAllowed = false; 0
1006 if (auto *I = dyn_cast(Inst)) 0
1007 VolatileIsAllowed = TTI.hasVolatileVariant(I, AddrSpace); 0
1008 ----
1009 if (auto *LI = dyn_cast(Inst)) 0
1010 return OpNo == LoadInst::getPointerOperandIndex() && 0
1011 (VolatileIsAllowed || !LI->isVolatile()); 0
1012 ----
1013 if (auto *SI = dyn_cast(Inst)) 0
1014 return OpNo == StoreInst::getPointerOperandIndex() && 0
1015 (VolatileIsAllowed || !SI->isVolatile()); 0
1016 ----
1017 if (auto *RMW = dyn_cast(Inst)) 0
1018 return OpNo == AtomicRMWInst::getPointerOperandIndex() && 0
1019 (VolatileIsAllowed || !RMW->isVolatile()); 0
1020 ----
1021 if (auto *CmpX = dyn_cast(Inst)) 0
1022 return OpNo == AtomicCmpXchgInst::getPointerOperandIndex() && 0
1023 (VolatileIsAllowed || !CmpX->isVolatile()); 0
1024 ----
1025 return false; 0
1026 } ----
1027 ----
1028 /// Update memory intrinsic uses that require more complex processing than ----
1029 /// simple memory instructions. These require re-mangling and may have multiple ----
1030 /// pointer operands. ----
1031 static bool handleMemIntrinsicPtrUse(MemIntrinsic *MI, Value *OldV, 0
1032 Value *NewV) { ----
1033 IRBuilder<> B(MI); 0
1034 MDNode *TBAA = MI->getMetadata(LLVMContext::MD_tbaa); 0
1035 MDNode *ScopeMD = MI->getMetadata(LLVMContext::MD_alias_scope); 0
1036 MDNode *NoAliasMD = MI->getMetadata(LLVMContext::MD_noalias); 0
1037 ----
1038 if (auto *MSI = dyn_cast(MI)) { 0
1039 B.CreateMemSet(NewV, MSI->getValue(), MSI->getLength(), MSI->getDestAlign(), 0
1040 false, // isVolatile ----
1041 TBAA, ScopeMD, NoAliasMD); ----
1042 } else if (auto *MTI = dyn_cast(MI)) { 0
1043 Value *Src = MTI->getRawSource(); 0
1044 Value *Dest = MTI->getRawDest(); 0
1045 ----
1046 // Be careful in case this is a self-to-self copy. ----
1047 if (Src == OldV) 0
1048 Src = NewV; 0
1049 ----
1050 if (Dest == OldV) 0
1051 Dest = NewV; 0
1052 ----
1053 if (isa(MTI)) { 0
1054 MDNode *TBAAStruct = MTI->getMetadata(LLVMContext::MD_tbaa_struct); 0
1055 B.CreateMemCpyInline(Dest, MTI->getDestAlign(), Src, 0
1056 MTI->getSourceAlign(), MTI->getLength(), ----
1057 false, // isVolatile ----
1058 TBAA, TBAAStruct, ScopeMD, NoAliasMD); ----
1059 } else if (isa(MTI)) { 0
1060 MDNode *TBAAStruct = MTI->getMetadata(LLVMContext::MD_tbaa_struct); 0
1061 B.CreateMemCpy(Dest, MTI->getDestAlign(), Src, MTI->getSourceAlign(), 0
1062 MTI->getLength(), ----
1063 false, // isVolatile ----
1064 TBAA, TBAAStruct, ScopeMD, NoAliasMD); ----
1065 } else { ----
1066 assert(isa(MTI)); 0
1067 B.CreateMemMove(Dest, MTI->getDestAlign(), Src, MTI->getSourceAlign(), 0
1068 MTI->getLength(), ----
1069 false, // isVolatile ----
1070 TBAA, ScopeMD, NoAliasMD); ----
1071 } ----
1072 } else ----
1073 llvm_unreachable("unhandled MemIntrinsic"); 0
1074 ----
1075 MI->eraseFromParent(); 0
1076 return true; 0
1077 } 0
1078 ----
1079 // \p returns true if it is OK to change the address space of constant \p C with ----
1080 // a ConstantExpr addrspacecast. ----
1081 bool InferAddressSpacesImpl::isSafeToCastConstAddrSpace(Constant *C, 0
1082 unsigned NewAS) const { ----
1083 assert(NewAS != UninitializedAddressSpace); 0
1084 ----
1085 unsigned SrcAS = C->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace(); 0
1086 if (SrcAS == NewAS || isa(C)) 0
1087 return true; 0
1088 ----
1089 // Prevent illegal casts between different non-flat address spaces. ----
1090 if (SrcAS != FlatAddrSpace && NewAS != FlatAddrSpace) 0
1091 return false; 0
1092 ----
1093 if (isa(C)) 0
1094 return true; 0
1095 ----
1096 if (auto *Op = dyn_cast(C)) { 0
1097 // If we already have a constant addrspacecast, it should be safe to cast it ----
1098 // off. ----
1099 if (Op->getOpcode() == Instruction::AddrSpaceCast) 0
1100 return isSafeToCastConstAddrSpace(cast(Op->getOperand(0)), NewAS); 0
1101 ----
1102 if (Op->getOpcode() == Instruction::IntToPtr && 0
1103 Op->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() == FlatAddrSpace) 0
1104 return true; 0
1105 } ----
1106 ----
1107 return false; 0
1108 } ----
1109 ----
1110 static Value::use_iterator skipToNextUser(Value::use_iterator I, 0
1111 Value::use_iterator End) { ----
1112 User *CurUser = I->getUser(); 0
1113 ++I; 0
1114 ----
1115 while (I != End && I->getUser() == CurUser) 0
1116 ++I; 0
1117 ----
1118 return I; 0
1119 } ----
1120 ----
1121 bool InferAddressSpacesImpl::rewriteWithNewAddressSpaces( 0
1122 ArrayRef Postorder, ----
1123 const ValueToAddrSpaceMapTy &InferredAddrSpace, ----
1124 const PredicatedAddrSpaceMapTy &PredicatedAS, Function *F) const { ----
1125 // For each address expression to be modified, creates a clone of it with its ----
1126 // pointer operands converted to the new address space. Since the pointer ----
1127 // operands are converted, the clone is naturally in the new address space by ----
1128 // construction. ----
1129 ValueToValueMapTy ValueWithNewAddrSpace; 0
1130 SmallVector PoisonUsesToFix; 0
1131 for (Value* V : Postorder) { 0
1132 unsigned NewAddrSpace = InferredAddrSpace.lookup(V); 0
1133 ----
1134 // In some degenerate cases (e.g. invalid IR in unreachable code), we may ----
1135 // not even infer the value to have its original address space. ----
1136 if (NewAddrSpace == UninitializedAddressSpace) 0
1137 continue; 0
1138 ----
1139 if (V->getType()->getPointerAddressSpace() != NewAddrSpace) { 0
1140 Value *New = ----
1141 cloneValueWithNewAddressSpace(V, NewAddrSpace, ValueWithNewAddrSpace, 0
1142 PredicatedAS, &PoisonUsesToFix); ----
1143 if (New) 0
1144 ValueWithNewAddrSpace[V] = New; 0
1145 } ----
